<div id="review_1135571640" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1135571640" />
    <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse"><img alt="Ms. Smartarse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401273675p2/13703358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1135571640?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Smartarse" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse">Ms. Smartarse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8704926-men-at-arms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=quotable">quotable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=racism">racism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=part_of_a_series">part_of_a_series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=politics">politics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1135571640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3490034535959594110">When I have first encountered the members of the City Watch, I rather disliked them. They were always misunderstanding everything due to missing about half of the big picture, and thus causing additional problems for the hero.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/62530.Thud___Discworld___34__City_Watch__7_' title='Thud! (Discworld, #34; City Watch #7) by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Thud!</a>, the first novel that I've read about them, didn't exactly endear the characters to me either. Oh I <em>liked</em> Angua: smart, pretty, with a 'mysterious' monthly affliction AND all-around dangerous aura; basically the epitome of a kick-ass heroine.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425734923i/13924988._SX540_.jpg' alt='Angua in Going Postal movie adaptation' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Thinking back on it, I'm g</span>
  <span id="freeText3490034535959594110" style="display:none">When I have first encountered the members of the City Watch, I rather disliked them. They were always misunderstanding everything due to missing about half of the big picture, and thus causing additional problems for the hero.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/62530.Thud___Discworld___34__City_Watch__7_" title="Thud! (Discworld, #34; City Watch #7) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Thud!</a>, the first novel that I've read about them, didn't exactly endear the characters to me either. Oh I <em>liked</em> Angua: smart, pretty, with a 'mysterious' monthly affliction AND all-around dangerous aura; basically the epitome of a kick-ass heroine.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425734923i/13924988._SX540_.jpg" alt="Angua in Going Postal movie adaptation" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thinking back on it, I'm guessing that I was also missing half of the big picture. Oh the irony of it all! Even though I could logically <em>understand</em> the inner jokes, I never ended up <em>caring</em> about any of the characters or their motivation enough.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64216.Guards__Guards___Discworld___8__City_Watch__1_" title="Guards! Guards! (Discworld, #8; City Watch #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Guards Guards</a> did a good job in introducing some of the main players, but some of the jokes still flew right over my head. I didn't particularly <em>like</em> Vimes, though Carrot's antics were always funny. Tall, strong, utterly naive, but struck by surprising insights at the right moment... he had <em>potential</em>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425734923i/13924989.jpg" alt="Carrot being tall" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/400354.Men_at_Arms__Discworld___15__City_Watch__2_" title="Men at Arms (Discworld, #15; City Watch #2) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Men at Arms</a> though, we get to see a wholly new side of Carrot. He has finally got used to Ankh Morpork and is now managing to charm each and every one of its inhabitants. His natural charisma just baffles everyone.<br><br><blockquote>
<br>‘He’s going to die, isn’t he,’ said Angua, quietly.<br>‘Funny, that,’ said Nobby. ‘If we was to try it, we’d be little bits of mince. But it seems to work for him.’<br>‘Krisma,’ said Sergeant Colon, who was having to lean on the wall.<br>‘Do you mean charisma?’ said Angua.<br>‘Yeah. One of them things. Yeah.’<br>‘How does he manage it?’<br>‘Dunno,’ said Nobby. ‘S’pose he’s an easy lad to like?’<br>
</blockquote><br><br>Speaking of character development, I am finally learning to understand the inner jokes about Corporal "Nobby" Nobbs. Although, I have to wonder why it took me two books. Perhaps I was skimming <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64216.Guards__Guards___Discworld___8__City_Watch__1_" title="Guards! Guards! (Discworld, #8; City Watch #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Guards Guards</a> too much. In any case, I can't wait to find out more about the Watch's resident weirdo.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425735674i/13925156._SX540_.jpg" alt="Corporal 'Nobby' Nobbs" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Another thing that I loved about this book, were the numerous one-liners. Not since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/48002.Thief_of_Time__Discworld___26__Death___5_" title="Thief of Time (Discworld, #26; Death, #5) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Thief of Time</a> did I feel the need to make a note of so many hilarious quotes.<br><br><blockquote>
<br>‘I’m a dwarf, too, but the dwarfs here don’t believe it.’<br>‘You don’t say?’ said Angua, looking up at him.<br>‘My mother had me by adoption.’<br><br>‘Don’t worry, miss,’ said Colon. ‘He-‘<br>‘Lance-Constable,’ said Angua.<br>‘What?’<br>‘Lance-Constable,’ she repeated. ‘Not miss. Carrot says I don’t have any sex while I’m on duty.’<br>To the background of Nobby’s frantic coughing, Colon said, very quickly, ‘What I mean is, lance-constable, young Carrot’s got krisma. Bags of krisma.’<br><br>‘It’s bad enough barging into Guild property, but we’ll get into really serious trouble if we shoot anyone. Lord Vetinari won’t stop at sarcasm. He might use’ - Colon swallowed - ‘irony.’<br>
</blockquote><br><br><strong>Score: 4/5 stars</strong> <br><br>A hilarious and thoughtful book about the Watch.<br><br>============================================<br>Other books featuring the Night Watch:<br>Review of the 1st book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/848814884" rel="nofollow noopener">Guards!Guards!</a><br>Review of the 3rd book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212951873" rel="nofollow noopener">Feet of Clay</a><br>Review of the 4th book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1313943620" rel="nofollow noopener">Jingo</a><br>Review of the 5th book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1319112593" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Elephant</a><br>Review of the 6th book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1319112623" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Watch</a><br>Review of the 7th book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/435878553" rel="nofollow noopener">Thud!</a><br>Review of the 8th book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1319112687" rel="nofollow noopener">Snuff</a></span>

<div id="review_1749999048" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1749999048" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1749999048?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1749999048" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11062242625513710326"><i>Men at Arms</i> is the second book in the <i>City Watch</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>. I liked this one better than the first book, <i>Guards! Guards!</i>. The story held my interest much better, and I enjoyed the characters more. Of course, it had a lot of the same characters as the first book, but I thought this one focused on more interesting characters. I like Carrot quite a bit, and we see a lot of him in this book. There are also two new members of the watch, Cuddy the Dwarf and Detritus (don’t salute!) the Tr</span>
  <span id="freeText11062242625513710326" style="display:none"><i>Men at Arms</i> is the second book in the <i>City Watch</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>. I liked this one better than the first book, <i>Guards! Guards!</i>. The story held my interest much better, and I enjoyed the characters more. Of course, it had a lot of the same characters as the first book, but I thought this one focused on more interesting characters. I like Carrot quite a bit, and we see a lot of him in this book. There are also two new members of the watch, Cuddy the Dwarf and Detritus (don’t salute!) the Troll, and I really enjoyed both of them.<br /><br />We saw less of Captain Vimes in this book, and that may actually be one of the reasons I enjoyed it more. So far he’s been a pretty morose character, quick to sink into despair and self-pity. He’s often off sulking (or in an alcoholic stupor) while everybody else is doing all the real work. He cares, I’ll give him that, but I prefer reading about characters like Carrot who care more effectively and less self-destructively. Carrot is a bit too perfect, actually, but I don’t mind because he’s fun to read about. Most of the Discworld characters are pretty over-the-top anyway, in one way or another, so he fits right in. <br /><br />I’m giving this 3.5 stars on BookLikes and rounding it up to 4 stars on Goodreads because I enjoyed it enough that I thought it deserved more than 3 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11062242625513710326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1259302232" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1259302232" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588746288p2/10326608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1259302232?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326608-lindsay?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326608-lindsay?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1259302232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3602324861586551797">Part of the Pratchett reread with the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2018. <br/><br/>The Night Watch is expanding with new watchmen being enrolled from the growing minority populations in the city of Ankh-Morpork. But at the same time, Samuel Vimes is looking towards retirement to marry Lady Sybil and become a gentleman of leisure, a future that the Vimes is struggling with. Then a series of murders involving a strange device from the Guild of Assassins occurs and the whole Watch is needed to deal with it.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64216.Guards__Guards___Discworld___8__City_Watch__1_' title='Guards! Guards! (Discworld, #8; City Watch #1) by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>G</a></span>
  <span id="freeText3602324861586551797" style="display:none">Part of the Pratchett reread with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2018. <br /><br />The Night Watch is expanding with new watchmen being enrolled from the growing minority populations in the city of Ankh-Morpork. But at the same time, Samuel Vimes is looking towards retirement to marry Lady Sybil and become a gentleman of leisure, a future that the Vimes is struggling with. Then a series of murders involving a strange device from the Guild of Assassins occurs and the whole Watch is needed to deal with it.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64216.Guards__Guards___Discworld___8__City_Watch__1_" title="Guards! Guards! (Discworld, #8; City Watch #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Guards! Guards!</a> set the scene for the Ankh Morpork City Watch, establishing how the police would work in such a world and some of the central characters. This book brings in more of the cast and establishes the ground rules for what Pratchett wanted to do with his series going forward, with themes of changing demographics because of immigration, racism in general ("speciesism" here) and the reality of policing from a Peelian principles philosophy but also conscious of the role of politics in general in all of that. That's a lot of weight to put on one book, but even so, it feels effortless in its execution.<br /><br />Notable is the introduction of Angua and her relationship with Carrot and the return of Detritus and Gaspode with Detritus in particular getting some excellent characterization. Angua is handled generally well, and her encounters with Gaspode are well done. I'm a little less thrilled about this as the origin of Angua and Carrot's long-running relationship and both Gaspode's perspective on it as well as the message that is Big Fido's character.<br /><br />Overall it holds up well to a reading in the modern day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3602324861586551797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3626386" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3626386" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3626386?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Sammis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Sammis" href="/user/show/122647-sarah-sammis">Sarah Sammis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552153164" href="/book/show/61651.Men_at_Arms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122647-sarah-sammis?shelf=pc">pc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3626386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10692310400593191649">Men at Arms is the second book I've read for the Beach Blanket Bonanza. My husband (whom I originally introduced to Pratchett's books) has been selecting the best of the Discworld books for me to read and I have been enjoying these reading "assignments" thoroughly.<br/><br/>Men at Arms is the next in the "Night Watch" group of books. Vimes is on the eve of his retirement from the watch and about to get married. Meanwhile, bodies are showing up in Ankh-Morpork and a new weapon has been stolen. Carrot and a</span>
  <span id="freeText10692310400593191649" style="display:none">Men at Arms is the second book I've read for the Beach Blanket Bonanza. My husband (whom I originally introduced to Pratchett's books) has been selecting the best of the Discworld books for me to read and I have been enjoying these reading "assignments" thoroughly.<br /><br />Men at Arms is the next in the "Night Watch" group of books. Vimes is on the eve of his retirement from the watch and about to get married. Meanwhile, bodies are showing up in Ankh-Morpork and a new weapon has been stolen. Carrot and a bunch of new recruits set out to solve the mystery and retrieve the weapon before all hell breaks loose.<br /><br />In Men at Arms, Pratchett sets aside the puns (for the most part) to work on world building and fleshing out his characters. Ankh-Morpork begins to feel like a believable working (as well as it ever does) city. Carrot grows as a character and is rapidly becoming one of my favorites (but then everyone likes Carrot).<br /><br />Best of all, there is an honest to goodness mystery (and hence plot) in Men at Arms. It was one of the best mysteries I've read this year with enough clues to get me close to solving it but still tricky enough for some surprises. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10692310400593191649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ue+GOBuw3/zUZZhiaVk40Rb/VnMWtAe5crAKS8ak70Frye/qoO4WlHNOLAOerDIOwKCxu9g5id4pzkz6C+cd2w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1235562205p3/1654.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">Terry Pratchett
</a></div>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18232416020196717902">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText18232416020196717902" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18232416020196717902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

A good man will kill you with hardly a word.&rdquo;</span>
